Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it up with bandages, then treat it until it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is swollen and full of pus, then pierce or open it lower down.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and blood flows out, then stop it, and bind it, and cauterize, for this is his trade.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the jugular vein, and the conduit is guarded, because that's where the blood goes,
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	if you cut the jugular vein on the side of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then hold it firmly, and let it rest for some days, then heal the wounds of the joints until they are healthy;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, seek it out;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, remove them gently so you can, and those that you cannot have, let them be until the wound festers;
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and be careful and adjust the outlet;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, powder it with the powder I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has become fistulous, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	from a wound of a spear or a dagger
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a blow from a spear or a dagger, and the wound is deep, then examine if the wound has become putrid, because you will know then that the patient is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh in all its blood, then do not put the powder on it at the first hour, nor bind it with a bandage that does not penetrate deeply,
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and inspect the body, and look at the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put attraction in the affected place, and apply it several times a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you don't have attraction, then put much cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture,
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound several days, or two, or three, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no spasm coming, nor evil trembling of heart which are not tokens of anguish;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good dispositions, then know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal the hand then with tents and other cures, so that it may be healthy;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal, and becomes an ulcer, then know that there is a fistula; if the treatment is done as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or in the chest or back, if the treatment of that which is in front;
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, of stitching; and if it is small, of powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has seized pieces, thus cauterize the wound, and remove foreign bodies if they are dislodged;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not dislodged, let the wound putrefy, thus lighten the extractions;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and of other wounds in other limbs, the judgments are as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Here is the translation:
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great and many and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the great wound often bursts the intestine, or the knots of the intestines, because of the intrusion from outside;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitching is more troublesome, and often a small wound is worse than a large one;
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because when we replace the intestines in, we do not put them back in order, from hot to hot;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	Because the intestines swell so much that they feel cold, if they return to points,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and because of this, it is necessary to treat the inner wound, because one must reset the intestine to its place like the others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is in four manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the common fractures often occur in the fracture of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the fracture of other wounds of the body and other proper fractures are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and they are more suitable with the bandage of the belly, and I will specify each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and none of the intestines are outside,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and grievous thing is to replace, this is by one of the ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	where the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	because of this the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is frosty, warm it in such a manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	soak a sponge or a cloth in hot water and apply it gently,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you cook in hot water steeping and macerating and soaking,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and raise the intestine as much as the swelling is reduced;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and many times they make these restraining vines, and it is necessary that they be loosened by unswelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling departing, then moisten the intestine with water or wine and evil humors are cooked,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for it is aligned to the entrance of the body by a small amount;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small wound at the instrument with which one collects the blood clots;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is to remove what is superfluous in size,
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we should not cut without great necessity that it be;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and these are the instruments for cutting:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut deeply into the curve and do not dig further, and see there the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines burst out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if you put it back in place according to its natural form in its proper location,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	see if you can put it in power, for that is worth miracles.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large and it is on the lower part beneath the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	it is necessary that you lay the patient on his back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and it is in the lower part beneath the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	If you set the head and the foot higher than the parts below,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also the rupture of the belly is in one of the injured parties
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	if you set it straight so that the injured part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus you must manage it as I say in great wounds and injuries.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Small wounds heal quickly when they are well-dressed.
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then put it between your hands, I mean minister carefully, you should hold the entire bandage in your hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring the lips together;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and that is the common way of suturing,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then let the head of the wound be, I give a space, and I fix a needle or it has, I have a strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and prick the two heads of skin with the two heads of the suture,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is beneath the skin within, so that you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and gather the four chief veins which siphon the humors; ensemble;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then strain through a double thread twisted around the needle of the vein, part by part,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then gather the four heads of the wounds approaching,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then let the two fingers of the span, and fix another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then thread the second filament as you did the first needle
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease from doing that according to what you have mastery of the needles
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wounds are closed;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the needles be moderate, between subtle and large,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because the subtle needles penetrate all the flesh, and the too large ones cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	because it is necessary that they be tempered;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not necessary to push the needles too deeply into the flesh and soft skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they do not penetrate and open up the wound before the suture;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut the heads of the veins, so they do not bother the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I hold taut or wrapped around the heads of the veins to keep them steady,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and let them be until the wound is sewn;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of cutting the veins is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because he suffers from a needle or an ulceration.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second wound is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you gather the ulcers of the skin and the ulcers of the flesh together into a needle or where there is a strong moist filament;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these wounds all together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	If you reset the needle to the part where you started, in the manner that one cuts the threads;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and place a space between each stitch the thickness of a smaller finger;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch follows the bone,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed up a wound that one had on the belly or stomach,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded by a razor,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm's width large,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it was nine palm's widths of intestine,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I restore the intestine then when it has been 23 hours without food.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was sewn up to 15 days, and it healed, and it was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctor had given up that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not heal him with ointments, for I was in a place where none were found, nor any medicines;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and apply a remedy more on the wound with much cotton frequently in the day, and wash it with honey water until he is healthy.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the proper ways of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and sew up the part that is deficient just up to the inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the right heart in the right direction, if you have sewn up the head of the suture or stitched or you have placed the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and let them pierce from another part of the inner side up to that defect;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this treatment is that you sew thus as the furrier makes the pelts,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and let one side of the suture remain for a while, and take it up again from another side, until the treatment is fully accomplished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of treatment, which Galen properly described,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	if it is thus as a certain spring, which naturally assembles the injured parts together.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and applies one head to the other head, in such a manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	fix a needle or head of a probe close by, and make it pierce the limb slightly,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and let the injured heads settle;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	Then turn the needle, and make it pierce the weak part just up to the dent inside.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as it reaches the head of the swelling;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce one and the other of the weak part just up to the dent inside, in the other heads of the swelling that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and it is the worst way of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Here is the translation:
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	One must cauterize the belly with two needles, or it has thread in each one;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one should push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is within the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	if it is a suture more grievous than other wounds of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the fresh wound in all its blood, thus the art has moved,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then reset the intestine, and the cut; then put on the powder irritating flesh,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and the art has moved it, then put on some ointment that is present, until the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and they inject the filament, and are sewn up the suture, and the scar.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound like the others, until it is healthy;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicines, put them on, as soon as it begins to gather pus, cotton much,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and remove it several times a day until it is healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you have no need of other medicine in many conditions when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not affect the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is necessary to apply a light ointment of tempered heat, or in a rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it between the joints, and beneath the spines;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if they feel pain or decay in the belly, and often happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if they are given a cluster of black wine immediately, and meanwhile the decay reaches just up to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and it pierces within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine which is called "jeune" cannot heal when it is wounded,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it is through the plant of the veins that they are, and through the subtlety of the whole body, and the approaching of its natural strength.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the wound's suture breaks, set it back as it was when the intestine is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and becomes black or dark, then you must lay the black lead that removes blood which does not come from life,
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then touch what is between the eyebrows,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and place the fingers pendant from the part below the wound up to the furthest point to ease the extraction when the nerves are cut, and the wound is swollen.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the eyeball
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is wounded, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if one cannot restore it in some homes,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that a man was pierced or wounded by a spear in his belly;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and thus blocked the evacuation and flatulence;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I will translate the sentence:
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him sweating, I doubted that the patient had a bad condition in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no point of pain, but he remained in better dispositions, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and certain experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied up in such a manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take firm stitches with large threads, then bring together the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the patient has opened their mouth, if they place it on the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	if they stretch their mouth upwards;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then they grasp the head, and it holds so that it cannot dislocate,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then place another finger afterwards in the same way as before, so that the wound is completely closed;
et cout la plaie.	and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If the head gets stuck in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can tie the intestine with a subtle thread that is cut from the intestine of a beast,
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	Take the head of this gut thread so it is well unravelled,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then attach it to the head of this thread, namely a subtly twisted flax thread,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then put the thread on the needle, and sew up the intestine, and reset it in its proper position;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching up the intestines is not forced except according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and large, especially when it is in one of the gut intestines, if there is no ingenious remedy, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes swollen, is universally called a "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and especially when it is split and torn apart.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And fistula is according to the true nodulation of hard and white, where one does not feel pain.
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also hairy like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it bursts out clear pus, and other times it thickens;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes a little, and other times enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have already spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not clean, and there is flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	it is not outside except by one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	it is to know, through the small passage of blood or course;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	where for this reason he has hard flesh within, and on the lips, that he does not let it grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	where he has too much of a bump;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	where the skin is porous, and the material is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	where the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	for this reason that the corruption is a kind of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	because the property in the region is slow in digestion, and slow in sanitation, and is weakened by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I teach you to know the treatment of fistula which is done by work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula has in all tender parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or in the spleen, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	where the spine of the back, or where a joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it is a part that comes to the property of the principal member, and similar limbs.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are of grievous healing, and there is no remedy but labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is no fistula that does not approach exactly to the place I have said, and you are confident of the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you examine the view, if you take a straight tent of iron or steel, so the fistula is upright, so the quarter;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, then search for a subtle tent of lead,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the leads bend into the twistedness;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many perforations and you cannot search well by tents,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if he is treated with a clyster through one of the passages,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for the moisture flows from one passage to another, and it becomes cloudy;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then you should carefully examine your power, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and it is shaved away at the front,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and the place where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I told you, if the wound follows what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the false growth and the rotten flesh that is within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then treat it until it is healthy,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well perforated in the right spot, then it is necessary that you cut around it, as much as you can.
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I put threads moistened with medicine in a liquid state, and the ends just at the head of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	so that the medicine corrodes the excess flesh which is remaining at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put ointments on the healthy skin, so that it may be healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if he is not healthy through that, then cauterize as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut around it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve is injured in principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then remove it so that the corruption is entirely removed,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then the treatment of things which are inflamed so much that they become healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healthy, and returns to its natural state as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you are not a liar just up to the fountain:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if it uncovers and searches as much as you are at the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all corruption, then restore the joint;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot come to it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can treat it with tongs.
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if the extraction is done with an instrument suited to that,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, so remove them all, do not leave a single one;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture makes you do the opposite, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	Here is the translation:
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot open them for an hour, then apply to the wound something producing pus.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it be until the abscess is ripe around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will have less difficulty with the bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as the thigh or leg,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you remove so much of the corruption as the blackness is all gone,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the corrupted flesh, and it comes just to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if you want to heal and cover everything up to the corruption, and then cure it as much as it is swollen;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred to a man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	if you take an example and help with your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of around thirty years, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came inside the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	so that the materials came to the leg, and it was inflamed with a large abscess, and there was no way to remove the cause by opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the mirror shows by their foolish pride as much as the abscesses open.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and they corrupt many materials, and become fistula, and they come from many holes that all flow with moisture and humidity of the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many mirrors show a cure within twenty years, and there is no wisdom in the art of hands,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	so that I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was cured,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and that which corrodes through the openings to a large body;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young man became red, and had a citrus color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I probed a tent in one of these openings, and then sought out all the openings,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that one vein came against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hurried then, and cut into one of the openings as much as I discovered a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption went up to the bone within;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I seized upon that which appeared to me as corrupted bone, and I believed there was no other corruption, except for that which I had seen.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with medicines applied in a long sequence, and could not solder.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I re-examine, and discover the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the continued corruption in the bone, and the ulceration, and then I treated it, and thought to reset the joint;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not do so much that I seized upon a part of the bone, and pulled it out with all its mass,
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored it with medicines; and it was healthy and sound immediately,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it does not allow to restart the work because of the weakness of the patient, who cannot suffer,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and for the fear of death that I have of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For the evacuation of blood is often excessive, but it was completely healthy,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and a hard crust formed on the bone, and it was of good disposition and had no harm or contradiction in anything, neither to the wing nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if a bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take the ligature, and hold it at the head of the bone that is open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and instruct him to extend it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another ligature of a thicker thread than the first ligature, and tie it on the flesh that is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stand upright, if you treat the corrupted flesh at the bottom,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh above the wound where you see swelling, so that the serum does not spread to the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and apply a hot iron or a cupping glass below the bone to cover the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and thus it is necessary to swell as one can see and feel the corruption, and to swell again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not appear nice, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	if it discovers the flesh entirely; then put the fire underneath,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then let one part be purified by the other, the corrupted area, and let the purification occur from the length of the corrupted area, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint, and purify the bone or where it touches another part;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the injured joints, there is no other anguish than to cover twice;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is a prick in the hand or a prick of the foot, it is very strong that thing,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but however it behooves you to inquire into that corrosion, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and the mondification in all the ways that you can, but so that the vein or the nerve does not make counter to you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and it is known that the incisors and the wisdom teeth, which cover these bones, are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance of the mouth.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and their subtlety, and their greatness and their smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and because of this it is necessary to prepare each similar aspect of the work with his instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and it is known that the work will show you the instrument about which you will have mastery, according to the knowledge of this art;
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the manners of the diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you prepare the instrument with which you will operate according to what is convenient for it.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The heads burst out or because of inwardness, or because of fervor;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have applied medicine to corrode through treatment with medicines, it does not benefit at all,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	if it is necessary to amputate that limb up to the place where the corrosion comes,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	if the patient escapes death through this, or through evil, which is greater, from the defect of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limbs turn black, as if they were burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and prick afterwards at the blackness, then goes that corrosion of limb to limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and take by all the body; if you hasten to cover,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and it is by the percussion of certain venomous beasts, like scorpions of the sea and vipers and similar,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is at the head of the finger, then cover it, and do not give it space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes just to the hand, if the cope reaches the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach just to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, if the cope reaches the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and it does not matter less remedies that the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and all thus done when the corrosion comes or foot: if it comes to the first joint, then the cope reaches after another joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, so treat all the foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up into the leg, so treat at the joint of the knee;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes from above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way to treat or soothe the limb is that you bind it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend one of the tendons downwards, and another minister the other tendon upwards,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you dissect the flesh that is between the two tendons at a spacious interval, so that the bone becomes uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cover or sew, and apply a layer of linen cloth to each part, so that the sewing does not touch the healthy flesh,
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and bring to the patient another lesion and abscess to be treated.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if the flow of blood comes when you operate, then cauterize the limb hastily.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	where you apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is accomplished,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the limb with a suitable ligature, and care for it until it is healthy;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you that he had a similar case in his own foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a blackness which seemed to be certain of fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corrosion went first into his finger by the toe, so much that it took over the whole toe;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to amputate the toe, and was healthy;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long afterwards the corrosion returned in his hand, and it came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put him on rebounding things after the purification of the body, and cannot stop the corrosions;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and it seems that I touched his hand, and I did not want, that I had hoped to rebound the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I doubted also that if I cut his hand, he would not die;
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the veins of the man were feeble; and he despaired all, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he stopped his hand, and was healthy;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not seen it happen otherwise except when one does another task, so one has need of it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Never does an abscess come on a clear skin, and it stays for so long that it makes a great gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they break and burst, and the pus jumps out, and the veins become empty, just like a vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin which is above is also as subtle as the draped delicate.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and does not touch near the bone, nor near the nerve, and such disease is called "healthy".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so prolonged that it reaches the bone in the front, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and you should cure it by cutting all around, and similarly when it is subtle, just like one dresses a wound;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not hesitate because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you find that the wounds are growing worse, and the corruption is not on the surface,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the wound is deep in the flesh, so the treatment with a cluster should be like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Observe if the wounds are large, and the abscess which is in them is of foul odor.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then theclysterization of Egyptian medicine which is thus made:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take aisil, and oil, and litharge, in equal measure, and put copper into the vessel over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and thickens as much as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take of this according to your need, and make it into a thin stream and in honey
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and cleanse the wound, and hold back the pus;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine sit for two hours, then extract it by expressing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the wound is made whole, and the pus is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and no time is it cleansed with water of ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes from the wood of a vine, and throw water on them,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then boil, and cleanse with it, until you know that the wounds are well purified;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot suffer it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	If they clysterize with water and honey or if they have a bit of liquid litharge broth;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you clysterize with honey and mild wine, which has the properties of cleansing and washing,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the wound dry;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you are certain that the wounds are well cleansed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if one cauterizes what makes the flesh grow in them,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and it is that you take a definitive plaster, and make it with oil of rose and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	where you cauterize with certain medicines and ointments, whose properties I have mentioned in the treatise on ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the pierced area of the sinew is small, and the canal of the cauterized area cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	If you enlarge a wound with an iron, and put there a tent of Egyptian ointment.
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or ointment of balsam, so that it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too large, then sew and let it heal thusly, or the cluster may enter afterwards.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the perforation that throws below is above, then cut around or lower than where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowel is in a state of fullness, do not let it burst forth suddenly;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot conceal the shame that is beneath, as you wish,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	it appears in such a manner that the bowel runs to the lowest place where it is,
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the bowel is full, do not let it burst forth suddenly
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the wound beneath thus as you saw,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	it appears in such a manner: that the bowel falls lightly downwards, and leaves nothing of the bowel;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and stretch over it a drapery of linen that covers the whole wound;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then apply force directly to the hole of the breast, which is a little larger at first,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then they are joined softly upon it, another dressing according to the quantity of the hole,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it on the hole of the breast to adjust the swelling, and do not remove the large dressing until after many days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and he who is above the hole of the breast, removes it frequently to reduce the swelling,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what runs from the bowel, whether it's venom or a little or enough, or digestive, or not digestive;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take heed of the patients who feel pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has been extended in such a way and you see the nature that jumps upon the tender part of the breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	if you know that the breasts are hurt, and approach the health;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then he dislocates it in the morning, or the third day, and when you delay the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	if you change to another dressing, and renew the bandage.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the wounds gape open indented after many days, know that the wounds have not closed yet.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if you come to subtle shortness of breath after long tension, do not despair of health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	because the saints approach. Because there are men who take long to heal their wounds, and of those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and it is a sign of indigestion if the belly swells above the umbilical area after many days, which means that the guts are not functioning properly;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the guts take time to digest, and it is sluggish, then you should add medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue;
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	as if it were a dialectical remedy, because there is a great part of vitriol, and it is the last resort medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Here is the translation:
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then apply the confection and use it; and this same thing makes honey cooked thick.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when we do not find any presence,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	where you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind them, and powder them over the honey when it is on the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then glue it to the dressing, and it stands on the wound, and no one administers it according to the rules of a long Aristologist;
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of the celestial body, which is also like a ferryman of voices and hundred.
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in use of simples or of compounds: crush them, and make into powder, and put on the honey that I have said, and in use;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the cure is prolonged, and it is not cured by this cure,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that the corruption is deep-seated, and makes an impression on the bone, or on the hard members, or on the ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess on the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panarice is an abscess that grows beneath the fingernail of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or at the foot, or which happens to grow in other toes;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is inflamed, and one does not take care, if it becomes a festering abscess.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they run and pour pus as far as the root of the nail, and by chance they corrupt the whole;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and there come the ulcers up to the bone, so that they bring foul pain, and it is the head of two long fingers, and the color is dark brown.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not profit at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	if it is necessary to cut for you the entire superfluity which remains on the finger,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterizers are of great aid if the bone is sound, and the finger is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the finger presses on the flesh inside, and it begins to point, and becomes white,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	it is necessary that you put the right treatment under the ankle which does not touch the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and the swelling above, and touch the subtle and light flesh,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and apply to the remaining flesh medicines that are burning and corrosive to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the joints so that they may be healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, so scrape, and draw forth fiercely, for as much as the bone is corrupted it is, if it cannot be healed;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the finger corrupting, so scrape in the same way as I have said before,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal it until it is healthy;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is festering, and swollen, and it feels great pain, so it is necessary that you heal it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the corner of the thumb, which is excessively thick when cutting across.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and beware that the cut does not reach the flesh which is beneath the thumb, for the patient would feel too great pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then apply something to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain that comes from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two joints that grow in the hands of some men by chance are entirely numb,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance they have a part where there is a bone, and sometimes they have a fingernail,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them grows in the root of the joint, where the birth is in some of our fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that grow on some node of the finger do not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those who are born with a thick finger, by chance it moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of the one who is lean is light, in such a manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born at the root of the joint are difficult to cure: if you hold two fingers.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born or ought to have a new nail, it is necessary that you first shape the round flesh up to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then shape the bone to a suitable joint for that, then heal it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sudden pains that come together in two ways arise from birth, or from the suddenness of a wound, or from burning by fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you shape that joint, so that the finger restores itself according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two tender tents or soft drapery moistened with rose oil, so they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two subtle pieces of thin lead, as long as the joint is swollen, as it is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	Stick them to one of these two with the palm, if you find that joint suitable as it is necessary.
Des vils	Of veins
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	You have thick veins full of superfluous melancholic humors that come from many parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they are more abundant in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you administer sometimes purging of the colon, and then the juice of the basil plant.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment of iron is according to two methods: one is that they are taken by cupping, and then the black blood is drawn out;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and another manner is that you lift the vein, and pull it out completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The incision should be made in this manner: first raise the leg high with a hot compress very strongly, so that the large vein is subtitled.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then stretch the leg of the patient downwards from the hip to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut into the vein in one, two, or three places, with a large incision.
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then release and draw the black blood from one vein to another, from one head to the other, as much as the patient's strength allows, like the virtue of the patient can suffer.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then the vein, and command that it be tied with black thread in a circular manner;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and restart the evacuation and the blood-letting when the veins are full, and do not annoy the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The elevations of the limb are according to this manner: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Then put him in a bath, and the thigh of warm water rises as it turns red, and inflates the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, heat it with fire, and then cover the area of the vein from the top of the thigh to the knee, or in the part below the joint;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the ankle, and scrape the vein of each part, until it appears when one feels it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you will see it red and black, and when it enters under the skin it seems like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then apply the treatment beneath, as long as it is elevated above the skin, and then place it on the slightly concave area
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cover it in another way, with two bandages; then strip the skin above the vein as much as it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it to the bone, as you have done, and place it on another concave area, as you had done previously;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cover with another bandage, or more if you have mastery of it, then lift it, and cover the toes of the foot
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then burn with fire up to the second joint; then extract at the joint, as long as it is entirely bare, then the scab.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot burn and lift, if you thrust a strong double-threaded needle everywhere.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and burn and cauterize, and you thrust underneath, and turn your hand from one side to the other, as long as it is sufficient;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and beware that it does not form a scab, for if it forms a scab, you cannot burn or lift, and it brings harm to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have treated it all, place on the spot of the painful wound a moist linen cloth soaked in wine and rose oil; and care for it until it is healthy.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the veins are constricted and twisted and entwined together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	so you must bend it gently, but do not cut it; and treat it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron tool with which one cuts the veins is curved, and does not cut too deeply, so that it does not cut into the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of large curvature, for if it was subtle, if it seized the vein, but so large as we have said, and this is the form.
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is engendered in legs, in warm parts where there grows no herbs nor tree, and in earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance grows another part than in legs, and this comes from the putrefaction that comes from under the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as it comes within the body of snakes and worms, you should distinguish between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And the signs of the beginning of this vein are if it comes into the leg a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the veins change, and the vein begins to issue forth, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head is open, it is necessary that you envelop it with a piece of cloth about one and a half inches to the joint, and the nail.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the splint remain on the leg, and every time it is not on the fracture, if the swelling envelops around the splint, and the tumor;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and envelop the remainder, and do not cut it in its root, until it is entirely removed;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it returns to the flesh, and causes an abscess and putrefaction in the limb, and a bad disease;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the head, and nothing remains in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and it is sometimes this vein when it is treated with five incisions of a hand's length, or ten.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and a man came to me, at whose hand it issued for ten inches in length, and when you cut it, if you prick or pierce, and penetrate just to the bottom,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	if all of it issues out; and let the material that is inside be emptied, and mix in the medicine that is given in a poultice to produce no pus for a day, then cure it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein runs into the marrow of the foot, and similarly when it opens into the joint of the foot, or where the foot.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and there comes much of perforations, and where it jumps veins; heal the wounds thus as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	From worms that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "ox disease", because it often affects the oxen.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the whole body, ascending and descending,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and feel well along the length of the limb from limb to limb, as long as they straighten the skin or it heals, and bursts forth;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is engendered by putridity of certain humors, if they come forth as worms and snakes and lice and roundworms or belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and doubt not of its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye;
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	perhaps it returns, and destroys the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see a patient who is wounded and troubled, if one cannot cure him quickly when he goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	it is necessary then that you bind the limb above and below with a strong well-stretched bandage,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut above and the arm falls, and if the vein is deeply in the flesh, and you do not find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you cauterize with fire above, until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that he causes, if it is that he corrupts the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or growing near the eye, hold the eyelid firmly in place, then cut above, and extract it completely;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the patient's purification of bodily medications with dissolving medicines for the bad humidors,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and beware of rotten foods that cause putridity.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes to some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then it moves from member to member; and I saw what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and I discovered a swollen arm, and saw a small inflammation in the vein of the arm;
